    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/214814351?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katy" href="/user/show/4572741-katy">Katy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer214814351" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7925614080155060803">I really thought this was going to be a good book, seeing how the summary was so interesting and people have been rating it pretty high. I'm not sure why. The plot had promise. I thought this book was going to have some intense romantic scenes (not as in sex, but as in chemistry) and some real action. Again, I was wrong.<br/><br/>I thought the characters in this book were BEYOND annoying. I didn't care of Jacque. I usually love fiesty characters with a temper and a sarcastic sense of humor. But she was ju</span>
  <span id="freeText7925614080155060803" style="display:none">I really thought this was going to be a good book, seeing how the summary was so interesting and people have been rating it pretty high. I'm not sure why. The plot had promise. I thought this book was going to have some intense romantic scenes (not as in sex, but as in chemistry) and some real action. Again, I was wrong.<br /><br />I thought the characters in this book were BEYOND annoying. I didn't care of Jacque. I usually love fiesty characters with a temper and a sarcastic sense of humor. But she was just TOO MUCH, to the point where every other line was a sarcastic remark. She tries to hard to be funny.<br /><br />And if Jacque is not bad enough, her two gossipy friends are worse, a bunch of squealing, bubblehead idiots, especially Jen. I know her character is made to be the one "who doesn't know when to shut her mouth," but she really just wears me out.<br /><br />The book uses too many sayings and catch phrases, and a lot of times, the characters are using them wrong on purpose. And there were too many uses of dog-related phrases. A couple of times is cute and clever. Throw in too many and you're just trying to hard. How many times do they need to say "throw me a bone?"<br /><br />I think the relationships between Jacque and Fane was too weird. I understand the love at first sight concept and the soulmates concept, but Jacque going back and forth really put me off. One minute, she's I'm not ready to be your mate, the next minute she's telling him she loves him in three days and wanting him to make love to her in less than a week. And she doesn't like PDA when he kisses her in front of everyone, yet he wants a very intimate part of bonding happen in front of her two girlfriends. How weird is that!<br /><br />I think the author tried to hard to make her characters witty and funny. I think if it had about 3/4 less of the trying, I might have really been able to enjoy the book. But it was too much, and it just ended up being really annoying to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7925614080155060803" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7865578903621989914">So, I know some people often rate books based on how realistic the characters and/or the dialogue is and this series may seem a bit far-fetched at first glance.   <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kitty (I solemnly swear that I am up to no good)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kitty (I solemnly swear that I am up to no good)" href="/user/show/16734001-kitty-i-solemnly-swear-that-i-am-up-to-no-good">Kitty (I solemnly swear that I am up to no good)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16734001-kitty-i-solemnly-swear-that-i-am-up-to-no-good?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16734001-kitty-i-solemnly-swear-that-i-am-up-to-no-good?shelf=did-not-finish-waste-of-time">did-not-finish-waste-of-time</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16734001-kitty-i-solemnly-swear-that-i-am-up-to-no-good?shelf=instilove">instilove</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer636246647" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13545580843651673453">Well I began this book because it was recommended to me...and it was free.<br/><br/>However I was unfortunately unable to get past the half way mark, now I really am a very patient reader and have got through some ludicrously cheesy plots/bad writing in the past (ahem <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/150038.Cassandra_Clare' title='Cassandra Clare' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cassandra Clare</a>.) Maybe this book was just not for me...or it got me on the wrong day, or maybe I should have given it another chance? Or maybe at twenty five years of age I am far to old to be reading this boring drivel.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380424623ra/846631.gif' width='400' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>When does this get g</i></span>
  <span id="freeText13545580843651673453" style="display:none">Well I began this book because it was recommended to me...and it was free.<br><br>However I was unfortunately unable to get past the half way mark, now I really am a very patient reader and have got through some ludicrously cheesy plots/bad writing in the past (ahem <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/150038.Cassandra_Clare" title="Cassandra Clare" rel="nofollow noopener">Cassandra Clare</a>.) Maybe this book was just not for me...or it got me on the wrong day, or maybe I should have given it another chance? Or maybe at twenty five years of age I am far to old to be reading this boring drivel.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380424623ra/846631.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>When does this get good...?</i><br><br><br><u>Things wrong with this book:</u> <br><br>Although the book started of in a vaguely amusing tone, with our heroine Jacque and a pair of binoculars stalking her neighbour's new overseas student, (CLICHE ALERT #1, I mean seriously...tall dark and handsome arrives right next door...BOKE. He arrives in a limo for fucks sake). <br><br>I was instantly hit with far too much info dumping...The main problem I have with this is, as well as being boring, they assume that as a reader we do not have the intellect to pick things up or work them out naturally as the story unfolds. Rather Loftis feels like she has to spell everything out to us, I know this is aimed for teens but most hormone ridden spot pickers are studying Hardy FFS! It also takes away any intrigue.<br><br>The unsubtle hints were just unbearable...like Ooooow Jacque's mother has weird feelings that sometimes turn out to be true, and sometimes Jacque can just tell from looking at somebody how they feel. Like for instance, if she is looking at their face and they are biting their bottom lip then she can tell that maybe they are worried or sad (or horny,) with out any words she just <i>knows</i>...(Anyway CLICHE ALERT #2 MC has mystery power of unknown limits. Do I give a flying fuck? No.) <br><br>As a personal taste I dislike this overly subjective, (and limited) third person narration. We are told in detail how Jacque feels about everything, I instantly felt uncomfortable at the awkward view point and began to wonder why not just narrate this in first person instead??? Aaaah...you also wish to give us Fane's POV well thanks for that little gem, but actually lets just forget his inane thoughts next time please? It just felt very unnatural. <br><br><i>"...Just a few hours ago I was just another 17 year-old getting ready to start my senior year, so normal she thought."</i><br><br>I beg your pardon? Maybe it is just badly edited but this is awkward writing on too many levels to even bother with. <br><br><br>So the story goes that Jacques new neighbour <u>speaks to her in her head,</u> and she just accepts this, she doesn't freak out and think she's going crazy or hide her spooky secret to find out some more info. Nope. She calls her pals and they <i>conveniently</i> believe her, and then <i>conveniently</i> appear in like seconds for a <i>convenient</i> sleepover. None of them really wonder WTF is going on, they are just like <i>'yeah he is such a hottie, lets get dressed and bring him southern food y'all and then we can discover why he is talking to you in you head.'</i> <br>Well, that is not believable. If you want to write good fantasy or whatever you have to make the natural human reactions to the supernatural believable over wise it all becomes unconvincing and boring.<br><br>Fane's thoughts were even worse. The thoughts he has are enraging. Firstly why really has he done this exchange, he is a werewolf from Romania (UGH CLICHE ALERT #3), would you allow your werewolf son to do this? No, because there are too many risks, I don't mean motorbike risky but more like people discovering the werewolf secret risky. <br>And yes he likes motorbikes, because he is a bad boy (CLICHE ALERT #4 'wannabe badboy') werewolf prince with tattoos. riiiight...<br><br>His inner monoglogues made furious rather than symapthetic...sympathetic made me think of the word pathetic which is a word that describes him quite well...AND THE THOUGHT HE SENDS HER??? GAH. <i>'At last my Jacquelyn'</i>, (CLICHE ALERT #5 THE DREADED INSTALOVE IS HERE) I mean seriously he is a teen boy right? So what does he mean at last? Really, how long has he been waiting? <br><br>Then there was just more info dumping...and then some really awkward conversations:<br><br><i>'"You must be tired from your long trip so why don't we show you your room and let you get settled for the night. If you are hungry, I can show you the kitchen and you are welcome to help your self to anything you find." Mrs. Henry stated.'</i><br><br>Stated? Really? Stated?! Just stick with 'said' for now ok? This is how people in those tapes you get teaching you English speak, not normal people welcoming a kid into their home. I thought Fane was foreign not her?<br><br>Then there was some more info dumping, and then there was the worst thing, just the worst thing: <br><br><i>'"Multumesc," he stated formally in his native tongue..."</i><br><br>Just fuuck off, ok? This is annoying and becomes even more so when he says he 'just forgets' sometimes and slips back into Romanian, but he is being formal and speaking to someone he has just met... So did he really forget, or is he just a pretentious twat??? It gets worse when the author puts a bracket beside the Romanian word for us silly dumb readers. For example: <br><br><i>"Good morning doemnelor (lady's), my name is Fane Lupei..."</i><br><br>I obviously wondered if Fane had actually said the English word 'lady's' in the bracket, and also why there was an apostrophe??? BUT then about a paragraph lower Lilly (sidetrack: Lilly is Jacque's mother who...you guessed it...is often absent CLICHE ALERT #6, absent parentals) asks Fane what <i>'doemnelor'</i> means and he told her it meant ladies. So what the hell was the point in putting it in brackets in his speech. Give us some fucking credit <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5014564.Quinn_Loftis" title="Quinn Loftis" rel="nofollow noopener">Quinn Loftis</a>, we can see you have worked out how to use google translate and that makes you very smart but there is no need to treat us like this.<br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380424623ra/846632.gif" width="400" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Well thanks for the... ughhh... head ache, I guess.</i></span>

<div id="review_370943609" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/370943609" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8630370-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/370943609?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/8630370-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer370943609" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11745673208191261000">When I saw the description of this book I was excited to read it. I will say I liked the story and it's idea. However, I didn't like the dialogue. It sounded corny, forced, and like something an inexperienced or fanfiction writer would write. I am not insulting fanfiction writers or the author in any sense but to me it sounded a little amateur when it came to how the characters interacted. It sometimes seemed as if they were trying to hard to be funny or sarcastic.<br/><br/>I found that while some of the </span>
  <span id="freeText11745673208191261000" style="display:none">When I saw the description of this book I was excited to read it. I will say I liked the story and it's idea. However, I didn't like the dialogue. It sounded corny, forced, and like something an inexperienced or fanfiction writer would write. I am not insulting fanfiction writers or the author in any sense but to me it sounded a little amateur when it came to how the characters interacted. It sometimes seemed as if they were trying to hard to be funny or sarcastic.<br /><br />I found that while some of the conversations were alright and realistic, others just left me thinking: Does anyone actually sound like this? My whole problem with this book was that I found it overly detailed in places that didn't really matter and that the dialogue was not doing it for me. Other than that it was an alright book. It's just that when I am reading a book I imagine what the characters voices would sound like in my head. So when I was reading this the characters sometimes sounded whiny, fake and sometimes annoying. <br /><br />They explained every little action in great detail and it sometimes got really annoying. For example:<br /> Jacque got a pan and put the rolls on it in straight rows; her mom had already pre-heated the<br />oven so she just put them in and set the timer for 7 minutes which is what the package directions<br />said. As her mom was stepping out of the room to call the Henrys she caught the briefest hint of<br />worry coming off her mom in subtle waves. It had been a while since she had picked anything up<br />from her mom so it kind of made her take a step back. I wonder what she is worried about?<br /><br />See? If she would have changed a few of the words and used contraction then it would have sounded more like a teenager and much more believable in my opinion. For instance, the last line says: I wonder what she is worried about? <br />Wouldn't it sound better if it read: I wonder what she's worried about.<br />See the difference an ' and a period can do? To me that shouldn't have been a question but a statement. Also, the punctuation and grammar in this wasn't really well done. I found many mistakes that could have been fixed or avoided all together since they were pretty obvious. I was actually disapppointed.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11745673208191261000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10886011989693825465" style="display:none">WOW this book is FANTASTIC!!!!!!!<br /><br />I absolutely LOVE Fane and Jacque together!!!!!<br /><br />Fane is a hot dominant Grey wolf from the Romanian pack. He decided to go to a different school for senior year as a foreign exchange student. He didn't know why he picked a high school in Coldspring, Texas. Just as Fane got out of his limo, to his host family's house, he heard a voice in his head. A female voice. The only thing that made sense was that he had a mate and his mate was near by. When he looked around he only saw green eyes looking from the window and a name, Jacque, said.<br /><br />Jacque Pierce is starting senior year in high school. Jacque found out a new foreign exchange student was moving right in front of her house. She needed to know who it was, if it was a he or a she, &amp; if he was hot or not. When a limo pulled up by the house she knew something was strange and when the he looked straight into her eyes it only got stranger. Then Jacque heard a voice in her head, a male voice, everything got extremely strange. She told Sally and Jen, her awesome best friends, about the guy who moved in. Sally and Jen were determined to meet the new foreign exchange student because they needed to see how hot he was for themselves. <br /><br />The next fine morning Jacque, Sally, Jen, and Jacque's mother went to the Henery's where Fane stayed for the school year. When Fane looked out the window, he knew who Jacque was in one second because of her amazing green eyes. Jacque was feeling a little weird and kinda wanted to leave. When someone opened the door, Jacque's eyes met with Fane's in just a second.<br /><br />This series is one of my favorite. I couldn't even put the book down. I LOVE Sally and Jen and how they both love Jacque. Fane is AMAZING in so many ways. Lastly, I Love how Fane is so protective of Jacque.<br /><br /><br />Five fantastic stars </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6799613713764677655"><b> 2.25 stars </b><br/>Yes, yes, you're wondering how I could give this book a low rating as "2.25" when I say I absolutely love this series, and when I go around recommending this to everyone I cross paths with. But that's just it people I love this "series" not this "book" and if you can get past this book, then this series is LOVE, but really please don't give up on this series just because of this book. <i> please </i><br/><br/>Okay, back to this book.   <span id="freeText6799613713764677655" style="display:none"><b> 2.25 stars </b><br />Yes, yes, you're wondering how I could give this book a low rating as "2.25" when I say I absolutely love this series, and when I go around recommending this to everyone I cross paths with. But that's just it people I love this "series" not this "book" and if you can get past this book, then this series is LOVE, but really please don't give up on this series just because of this book. <i> please </i><br /><br />Okay, back to this book. Now I re-read this for the sole purpose of reviewing this, so here we go.<br /><br />I love the whole Soul Mate's trope, it is my thing, and I remember continuing this series because of the soul mate trope, BUT THIS BOOK IS CRAP, I'm sorry but it is. I bear with reading the first book in this series only ONLY for Jen and Sally. <br /><br />Why this book is crap you ask?<br />Mildly tolerable crap may I add?<br />o <b> FANE </b> Okay people don't get me started on this idiot. Let me clear some things up, so this guy is 17, the male lead of THIS book, and the mate of Jacque and all that yada-yada bullshit. THIS GUY ID 17 AND IS MORE FORMAL THAN ACTUAL PEOPLE IN THIS BOOK THAT ARE CENTURIES OLD. You people might not view this as a major problem BUT IT IS A MAJOR PROBLEM FOR ME OKAY?<br /><blockquote> <i> <b> "At last, my Jacquelyn." </b> </i> </blockquote><br />Okay, first off that is creepy as fuck (because he says that in her mind two seconds after meeting her etc etc. Calm down people this isn't a spoiler, it was literally on the first page, okay?)<br />SO FREAKING FORMAL<br /><blockquote> <b> <i> "Thank you Jacquelyn, you are right. It will make me feel much better if you would come back in." </i> </b> </blockquote> <br />SO FREAKING FORMAL<br />Don't worry I'll spare you from all of the formal stuff he says (which is everything he says so yeah)<br />And, Fane, could you PLEASE SPARE ME FROM RANDOM TALKS BOUT YOUR OBSESSION WITH WILLIE NELSON, I DON'T WANT TO KNOW.<br />*sigh* I'll spare you from my rant about HIM now.<br /><br />o <b> The romance </b> Like????? I don't even ship Jacque and Fane??? I don't care for either of them actually????? Get out of my face. I'm not kidding, I don't even care for them in the later books <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Now if there is a romance plot line I DO care about it is JEN AND DECEBEl and COSTIN AND SALLY  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />o <b> JACQUE </b> I don't hate her, but I can't bring myself to care about her. *shrugs*<br /><br /><b> REASONS I TOLERATE THIS BOOK </b><br />o Jen<br />o Sally<br />o J E N<br />o S A L L Y<br />o J<br />o E<br />o N<br />o S<br />o A<br />o L<br />o L<br />o Y<br />honestly I love these two so much, it hurts???????<br /><br /><b> E X H I B I T: A </b><br /><blockquote> <b> <i> "Fane, seriously dude, You have a great backside, but I don't think this is really the time for me to admire it so could you please get your royal butt out of my face?" OHMYGOD I LOVE THEM SO MUCH.<br />*patiently waits for Costin and Peri in the next books*<br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1242652-cari?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1242652-cari?shelf=ya">ya</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer872997387" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8525662243719041239">Hey, Loftis? It's "duct tape", not "duck tape". <b>*facepalm*</b><br/><br/>How in heaven does this have a 4+ rating?<br/><br/><b>*falls over laughing*</b><br/><br/>I'm giving this book two stars instead of the single one it deserves because it lands solidly in "so bad it's good" territory. Bad enough that I kept reading because I enjoyed making fun of it. Probably not a reason why an author wants an extra star for but so be it, she should've written a better book.<br/><br/>And oh my God, <u>Prince of Wolves</u> is ever so awful--<i>laughably</i> awful. I read th</span>
  <span id="freeText8525662243719041239" style="display:none">Hey, Loftis? It's "duct tape", not "duck tape". <b>*facepalm*</b><br /><br />How in heaven does this have a 4+ rating?<br /><br /><b>*falls over laughing*</b><br /><br />I'm giving this book two stars instead of the single one it deserves because it lands solidly in "so bad it's good" territory. Bad enough that I kept reading because I enjoyed making fun of it. Probably not a reason why an author wants an extra star for but so be it, she should've written a better book.<br /><br />And oh my God, <u>Prince of Wolves</u> is ever so awful--<i>laughably</i> awful. I read the entire thing giggling all the way but rest assured, I was laughing <i>at</i> it, not with it. <br /><br />I fell in love with the premise as soon as I read the summary, as love stories wrapped in possessive, obsessive mating behavior are an instant hook for me, and within seconds I was on Amazon to download. I started reading the same night and within a page knew the book was in trouble: terrible writing, paper thin characters, and cringe-worthy dialogue, the perfect example of why authors need to read their work out loud. Loftis would've realized how terrible it was and perhaps corrected herself, and I wish someone made her spend some time around actual teenagers so she'd write how they really talk, not this nonsensical presentation. I'm not much younger than Quinn Loftis but still recognize their speech as missing the mark by not just miles but entire universes. There's no sense of urgency as you read, character reactions to events are completely unrealistic (they don't even blink when the whole "werewolf" thing comes to light), none of the characters display any consistency, the writing itself is downright embarrassing, and did I mention that the dialogue is <i>really bad</i>?<br /><br /><i>Note to the author:</i> if you have to tell me at least once per chapter that your characters are soooo sarcastic, then your characters aren't sarcastic. Stop telling me and give me good, snarky dialogue that doesn't sound forced and falls flat. Better yet, just give me dialogue that doesn't suck.<br /><br />The need for a copy editor made me twitchy. As my gift to the author, I'll start her on the path to better writing with this little tip: 's is possessive while a simple s on the end signals multiples. So if you're referring to more than one Grey then it would be Greys, not Grey's. And if a Grey owns something, then it's Grey's, not Greys. Got it? For fuck's sake.<br /><br />Overall I'm so disappointed with this novel, Loftis started with a fabulous plot and completely jacked it up. I'm sad for her and thankful this was free to download.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8525662243719041239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xGp2TX2z2kOUPYWgspyQf/06GQ85ikigifya//D+jBAPAsIDdhqEcqKQmr/D8BI2UM8suMfKriBQQDVUtjBeFQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ApQ+NSfkr2FpSQOFPUxqNtwXaQYGWcTjxoxJIZeESF7J/Ip7LE3xUF/kHJpMIOh/ceJcsfgZImMfMOaK0UqaWw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1647885138938355178">Hello, Readers. My name is Quinn Loftis and I am lucky enough to call myself a novelist. In 2011, I self-published my first novel, Prince of Wolves with no expectations, other than my friends and family might purchase the book out of pity. Now, several years later, with 30+ novels and counting under my belt, Prince of Wolves had been downloaded over 1 million times. Though I was hesitant at the ti</span>
  <span id="freeText1647885138938355178" style="display:none">Hello, Readers. My name is Quinn Loftis and I am lucky enough to call myself a novelist. In 2011, I self-published my first novel, Prince of Wolves with no expectations, other than my friends and family might purchase the book out of pity. Now, several years later, with 30+ novels and counting under my belt, Prince of Wolves had been downloaded over 1 million times. Though I was hesitant at the time to submit my work to the world for their scrutiny, I'm so glad I did. It made my dream of making a living by telling stories a reality. <br /><br />I'm blessed to share my household my wonderful husband of more than twenty years (who also co-writes with me on occasion), three beautiful sons, a French Bulldog, and an oversized tabby cat. I love hearing from readers, so if you have any questions about the books or my journey, don't hesitate to hit the 'Contact Quinn' in the menu above. Thank you so much for taking a chance on my books.</span>
